Title: Twisted Bilayer Graphene Lifetimes At Integer Fillings: An Analytic Result

## Twisted Bilayer Graphene Lifetimes At Integer Fillings: An Analytic Result 

Haoyu Hu ‚Ä†,1 Yuelin Shao ‚Ä†,2 Lorenzo Crippa, 3 Dumitru Cňė alugňė aru, 1, 4 Giorgio Sangiovanni, 3

Tim Wehling, 5, 6 Leonid I. Glazman, 7 and B. Andrei Bernevig 1, 2, 8, ‚ąó

Institut f¬® ur Theoretische Physik und Astrophysik and W¬® urzburg-Dresden Cluster of Excellence ctd.qmat, Universit¬® at W¬® urzburg, 97074 W¬® urzburg, Germany

IKERBASQUE, Basque Foundation for Science, Bilbao, Spain 

Twisted bilayer graphene near integer fillings hosts correlated single-particle excitations whose dispersion and linewidth are increasingly accessible experimentally. We study these excitations using the topological heavy-fermion model, which captures both strong correlations and band topology of twisted bilayer graphene. In the decoupled limit, where both the single-particle f c hybridization and the Hund‚Äôs coupling between f and c electrons are absent, the model admits exact solutions in which free Dirac fermions coexist with interacting f electrons that form zero-width Hubbard bands. By treating the f c hybridization and Hund‚Äôs coupling perturbatively around this solvable limit, we obtain analytical results for the single-particle self-energy. From the resulting self-energy, we derive explicit expressions for both the dispersion renormalization and scattering rates of both Hubbard-band excitations and low-energy Dirac modes, thereby establishing an analytical framework for understanding correlated excitations in twisted bilayer graphene. We analyze the scattering of the two kinds (őď 3 and őď 1,2) of Dirac electrons, and find that it has different mechanisms. We briefly investigate the effect of strain. We compare these analytical expressions with DMFT results on the same model. 

Introduction .‚ÄĒ Twisted bilayer graphene (TBG) near the magic angle [1] exhibits correlated phenomena [2‚Äď 32], unconventional superconductivity [9‚Äď12, 33‚Äď38], and exotic quantum phases [39‚Äď55]. Extensive theoretical efforts have been devoted to unraveling the rich phe-nomenology of magic-angle TBG. These studies span the development of models[1, 56‚Äď107], investigations of cor-related insulating and metallic phases [38, 98, 99, 108‚Äď 171], and analyses of unconventional superconductivity [111‚Äď114, 116, 119‚Äď121, 136, 160, 172‚Äď209]. Beyond stud-ies of ground states and ordered phases, recent quantum twisting microscope experiments also provide direct ac-cess to both the dispersion and the linewidth of excita-tions [210, 211]. This raises a central question: what mi-croscopic processes control the lifetime of single-particle excitations in TBG, and can they be understood analyt-ically? This problem is challenging because TBG combines two ingredients whose interplay is inherently difficult to treat: strong correlations and nontrivial band topol-ogy. The extreme flatness of the moir¬ī e bands makes electron-electron interactions the dominant energy scale, while the bands themselves retain topological structure. TBG therefore provides a setting in which topology and strong correlations are inseparably intertwined. A nat-  

> ‚ąóbernevig@princeton.edu
> ‚Ä†These authors contributed equally to this work.

ural framework for describing this physics is the topo-logical heavy-fermion (THF) model [212‚Äď214]. In this picture, localized f electrons subject to strong Hubbard interaction coexist with dispersive c electrons forming Dirac nodes. The nontrivial band topology arises from their hybridization. Within the THF framework, sub-stantial theoretical efforts, encompassing both analytical and numerical approaches, have been devoted to under-standing correlation effects in TBG [212, 214‚Äď224]. A key advantage of the THF model is that it admits an exactly solvable decoupled limit when both the f c 

hybridization and the Hund‚Äôs coupling between f and 

c electrons vanish [223, 225], provided that all density-density interactions other than the onsite Hubbard inter-action of f electron are treated at the mean-field level, as discussed in the next section. In this limit, free Dirac c

fermions coexist with interacting f electrons that form lo-cal moments and zero-width Hubbard bands. This solv-able point provides an analytical foothold for a controlled treatment of correlated excitations. It also makes it pos-sible to controlably ask how the sharp excitations of the decoupled problem are broadened once the two sectors are weakly recoupled. In this letter, we develop such a controlled expansion in the zero-temperature limit. Treating the f c hybridiza-tion and Hund‚Äôs coupling perturbatively around the ex-actly solvable decoupled limit, we derive analytical ex-pressions for the single-particle self-energy at integer fill-ings. These results allow us to determine both the dis-persion renormalization and the scattering rates of the 

> arXiv:2604.14303v1 [cond-mat.str-el] 15 Apr 2026

2

FIG. 1. Single-particle excitation spectra at integer fillings 

őĹ = 0 , ‚ąí1, ‚ąí2 (top to bottom), obtained within the Hubbard-I approximation (left), hybridization expansion (middle), and DMFT (right). To match the DMFT results, we evaluate the hybridization function Eq. (11) using a reduced effective hybridization parameter őļef f = őļ/ 4. 

Hubbard-band excitations and of the low-energy Dirac modes. We show that f c hybridization shifts the Hub-bard bands toward the Fermi energy. This is consistent with the DMFT results [217, 218, 226] and shows that the Hubbard-band separation is not precisly U but can be heavily renormalized. The f c hybridization also gen-erates a finite lifetime. For gapless modes near őď, f c 

hybridization renormalizes the Dirac dispersion and in-duces a scattering rate that is linear in |k| in the flat-band limit [212], while producing a finite scattering rate away from the ideal flat-band limit. Additionally, we ob-tain the dispersion renormalization and damping rate of the low-energy Dirac node induced by Hund‚Äôs coupling. Our results (Fig[1] and Table[I]) provide a transparent analytical framework for single-particle excitation life-times in TBG and a direct complement to numerical ap-proaches such as dynamical mean-field theory (DMFT), with which we compare. 

Model .‚ÄĒ We employ the THF model for TBG [212], which captures the coexistence of strongly correlated lo-calized f electrons and dispersive Dirac c electrons. Un-less noted otherwise, all results in this work are obtained at zero temperature. The system is described by the following Hamiltonian (see Appendix II of the Supple-mentary Material (SM) [227])

In contrast to Hcf , the Hund‚Äôs coupling acts on the őď 1 ‚äē őď2 sector of the c electrons rather than the őď 3 sector. Throughout this manuscript, we use the parameter val-ues reported in Ref. pő©M /ŌÄ ‚Čą 122 meV, where ő© M is the area of the moir¬ī e Brillouin zone. The other relevant en-ergy scales are the Hubbard interaction U1 = 57 .95meV, the f c hybridization strength ő≥ = ‚ąí24 .75meV, the Hund‚Äôs coupling J = 16 .38meV, and M = 3 .69meV. This hierarchy implies that local f -electron correlations are strong, while the hybridization and Hund‚Äôs coupling act as the leading perturbations governing the linewidths. However, our results turn out to be identical to those obtained in the opposite limit [228, 229] suggesting- as mentioned in [223], that the THF results are not strongly dependent on the ratio U/ő≥ , due to the light fermion lin-ear dispersion. 

Decoupled limit .‚ÄĒ We begin from the exactly solvable limit ő≥ = J = 0 [223, 225], which provides the sharp excitations that are broadened once hybridization and Hund‚Äôs coupling are restored. In this limit, the c and 

f sectors decouple, and both the ground state and the single-particle spectrum are obtained analytically. We focus on integer fillings őĹ = 0 , ¬Ī1, ¬Ī2, for which the ex-act ground state places all charge in the localized sector: 

őĹf = őĹ and őĹc = 0 [see the inset of Fig. 2]. For simplicity we take ŌĶc, 1 = ŌĶc, 2, which is exact at őĹ = 0. The c sec-tor then hosts a Dirac node pinned at the Fermi energy, with linear dispersion for M = 0 and quadratic disper-sion for MŐł = 0 [Fig. 2(a,b)]. The localized f electrons form free local moments [223], producing atomic Hub-bard bands. The corresponding charge-¬Ī1 excitations occur at energies ‚ąÜ ¬Ī1 (Appendix IV of the SM [227]) and satisfy ‚ąÜ +1 + ‚ąÜ ‚ąí1 = U1 [Fig. 2(a,b)]. The exact f -electron self-energy is local and diagonal in orbital, valley, and spin: ő£f,őĪő∑s,őĪ ‚Ä≤ő∑‚Ä≤s‚Ä≤ (iŌČ, k)

(11) Detailed derivations of Eqs. (9) and (11) are given in Appendix IV of the SM [227]. It is worth noting that Eq. (8) is different from the hybridization function used in DMFT calculations of the THF model. DMFT takes indeed the effect of the other lattice sites of the periodic Anderson model into account via auxiliary bath fermions that are self-consistently ad-justed [231‚Äď234]. 

Correlated single-particle spectra .‚ÄĒ Using the self-energy and hybridization functions in Eqs. (7) and (11), we obtain the single-particle spectra shown in Fig. 1 (de-tailed in Appendix V of the SM [227]). For compar-ison, we also show spectra from DMFT [232] and from the Hubbard-I approximation [223], where the f -electron self-energy takes the atomic form ő£ f, loc (iŌČ ) in Eq. (6). To align the hybridization-expansion results more closely with DMFT, we use the same parameters as in Ref. [232], including finite M and v‚Ä≤

> ‚čÜ

, but evaluate the hybridiza-tion function Eq. (11) with a reduced effective hybridiza-tion parameter őļef f = őļ/ 4 (numerically realized by dou-bling the c-electron bandwidth, corresponding to taking 

vef f ‚čÜ = 2 v‚čÜ in the hybridization function). Fig. 3 shows line cuts of the hybridization-expansion spectra near K

and őď, taken along the green and blue dashed paths in Fig. 1. The results from using the original őļ are provided in Appendix V of the SM [227] for reference. Within the Hubbard-I approximation, the f electrons contribute atomic Hubbard bands through ő£ f,loc (iŌČ ), while the bare lattice hybridization mixes these states with the dispersive c-electron bands. At this level, all excitations remain sharp and undamped. Including the leading self-energy correction from the hybridization ex-pansion, Eq. (7), produces two effects: an additional renormalization of the dispersion and a finite linewidth.        

> FIG. 3. Line cuts of the hybridization-expansion spectra near
> K(top) and őď (middle), taken along the green and blue dashed paths in Fig. 1. The bottom panel shows a zoom-in of the low-frequency spectra near the őď point. From left to right, the three columns correspond to őĹ= 0, ‚ąí1, and ‚ąí2, respectively.

As shown in Fig. 1, these leading-order results qual-itatively reproduce the corresponding DMFT features across integer fillings, indicating that the expansion al-ready captures the microscopic origin of the damping and band renormalization. The quantitative reproduction of DMFT requires a lower őļ. The justification for introduc-ing the effective őļef f is discussed in the next section. 

Analytical results for the spectra .‚ÄĒ We now derive the corresponding dispersion renormalization and scattering rates analytically. We focus on charge neutrality, őĹ = 0. Using Eqs. (7), (9), and (11), we determine the excitation energies and scattering rates from the poles of the Green‚Äôs function analytically. We focus on the Hubbard bands near the Brillouin-zone edge and the gapless modes near őď (see Appendix VI of the SM [227]). Near the Brillouin-zone edge, the f electrons form Hubbard bands at energies ¬ĪU1/2 within the Hubbard-I approximation. Including the self-energy correction induced by hybridization, the Hubbard-band energy is renormalized to

Through HJ , these fluctuations generate a self-energy correction for the őď 1 ‚äē őď2 c electrons [Eq. (5)]. Introduc-ing the dimensionless coupling

Summary and Discussion .‚ÄĒ We have addressed sev-eral experimentally important questions for the interact-ing bands of TBG: (1). At what energy are the Hubbard bands. We find Eq(12) a renormalization to lower values, consistent with DMFT, and which should be considered in future analysis of QTM experiments. (2) How sharp are the light c-electron excitations around the őď- point? We find two mechanisms, for the two types of light elec-trons: the hybridization between f and őď 3-type c elec-trons is responsible for their linear in k lifetime (Eq(15)) in the flat band limit or their finite (Eq(17)) small con-stant scattering for finite bandwith. By contrast, the Hund‚Äôs coupling J is responsible for the linear scattering rate of the őď 1,2 electrons (Eq(20)) in the flat band limit. Our hybridization method valid for ő≥ < U gives almost identical expressions with the projected THF method 

ő≥ > U [228, 229]. As suggested in [223], the relevant ra-tio is between U and the hybridization function at ŌČ = U .Since the hybridization function contains the DOS of a Dirac fermion and is proportional to ŌČ, the U cancels out, and the THF model is valid in both limits. We can further ask: what value of U would we obtain if we plugged in the experimental separation of the Hubbard bands [210] in Eq(14). The answer is U = 64 meV, higher that the values used in all literature so far, and higher than the energy splitting in [210]. This urges caution in interpreting the energy splitting of the Hub-bard bands in [210] directly as U . The Hubbard band spacing renormalizes from U to lower values Eq[14]. Our work demonstrates that the solvable THF limit offers a systematic analytical route to correlated excitation dy-namics in moir¬ī e systems, qualitatively complementing numerical approaches such as DMFT but still showing their need for quantitative agreement with experiment. We note that DMFT [217, 233] spectral function agrees with [210] without tuning, and with parameters U, ő≥ that are computed from microscopics [212].

Appendix I: Summary 

In this note, we investigate self-energy corrections generated by the single-particle f c hybridization and by the 

f c interaction, namely the Hund‚Äôs coupling term HJ . Accordingly, two small parameters are introduced to perform systematic series expansions in each case: 

őļ = ő≥2

őļ = 0 .013 , j = 0 .006 (S2) The results at charge neutrality ( őĹ = 0) are summarized in Table S2.

a. Symmetries of the hybridization function 

As shown in Eq. (S6) to Eq. (S9), the flavor U(8)-symmetric local hybridization function ‚ąÜ( iŌČ ) keeps the spin SU(2), valley U V (1), C3z , C2x and C2z symmetries. Here we show that the hybridization function ‚ąÜ M (iŌČ ) derived in Eq. (S150) also preserves the particle-hole symmetry and time-reversal symmetry. The local self-energy Eq. (S11) respects the particle-hole symmetry P : ‚ąÜ +1 ‚ÜĒ ‚ąÜ‚ąí1, n f ‚Üí (Nf ‚ąí nf ) as

Appendix V: Numerical results 

using the self-energy derived in Eq. (S138), we can also obtain the Green‚Äôs function and the corresponding spectral functions numerically. In Fig. S4, we illustrate the spectral function with the Hubbard-I approximation (Eq. (S137)) and the result from the hybridization expansion (Eq. (S138)) at integer filling őĹ = 0 , ‚ąí1, ‚ąí2. In Fig. S4, we have used the full model with finite M and v‚Ä≤

> ‚čÜ

.Several general remarks are in order. First, the self-energy at order ő≥2 renormalizes the Hubbard-band energies, shifting them toward the Fermi level. Second, the self-energy introduces finite damping of the Hubbard bands. These trends are qualitatively consistent with the DMFT results reported in Ref. [232]. In addition, both Hubbard bands at őĹ = 0, the lower Hubbard bands at őĹ = ‚ąí1 and őĹ = ‚ąí2 are strongly damped and are barely seen in the figure, again in qualitative agreement with the DMFT results of Ref. [232].

Appendix VII: c-electron self-energy from f c interactions at charge neutrality őĹ = 0 

In Appendix III of the SM [227] to Section VI, we focused on correlation effects arising from the Hubbard interaction 

U1, treating the hybridization ő≥ perturbatively and retaining contributions up to order ő≥2. This correlation effects 72 first generate a dynamical self-energy for the f electrons, which subsequently contribute to the damping rate of the hybridized bands. In this section, we turn to correlation effects induced by the f c interactions HJ and HW , which will also generate a dynamical self-energy and finite scattering rate. We begin in the zero-hybridization limit, where the f c interactions are treated at the Hartree-Fock level previously. (Although when calculating the hybridization function, we take the approximation W1 = W2 and J = 0 to get an analytic formula. While in the other parts, the HF contribution of 

HJ is kept.) We then incorporate dynamical correlation effects generated by the f c interactions by expanding the self-energy to second order in the f c interaction strength, with the first-order term corresponding to the Hartree-Fock contribution. Throughout this section, we set ő≥ = 0 and focus on charge neutrality to simplify the analysis. Since, in the ő≥ = 0 limit, the low-energy gapless excitations are formed by the c electrons, we focus on the self-energy of the c

electrons. We consider a generic f c interaction taking the form of

Physically, the self-energy correction arising from the J term acts on the őď 1 ‚äē őď2 electrons, which are already gapped by the M term. As a result, the gapless mode formed by the őď 3 electrons does not experience a strong damping effect near őď point. As a comparison, the gapped modes n = 2 , 3 formed by őď 1 ‚äē őď2 electrons do have a finite damping rate at őď point. At charge neutrality, the damping rate reads 1

3. Effect of strain 

In Eqs. (S33) and (S34), we proved that at low temperature, only the őď 1 ‚äē őď2 c electrons acquire a dynamical self-energy at order j ‚ąľ J2 due to the local-moment fluctuations of f electrons. Thus, we expect that if the local-momentum fluctuations are quenched, the damping rate will also be suppressed at order j. To verify this, we investigate the effect of finite strain, which will frozen the local-momentum fluctuations at charge neutrality in the low-temperature limit. For simplicity, we focus on the case of M = 0. 86 The strained Hamiltonian of the f sector takes the form of

őł(|ŌČ| ‚ąí 2őĶ)őł(|v‚čÜőõc + 2 őĶ| ‚ąí | ŌČ|) (S106) We can observe that, the scattering rate of the c electrons (Im[ő£ c(k, ŌČ ‚ąí i0+)]) vanishes at low-energy limit with 

|ŌČ| < 2őĶ. When a finite strain is applied, the fluctuations of the f electrons are quenched at low temperatures, because the f -electron ground state becomes non-degenerate in the atomic limit. In the absence of low-energy f -electron fluctuations, the scattering rate is correspondingly suppressed and approaches zero.
